9:30 After a big first patch. PS5 has 4 Performance modes.  Performance - 1080p upscaled to 4k using FSR, up to 120hz  Balanced (the one I use) - 1269p upscaled to 4k using FSR, at stable 60hz  Quality - upscaled 4k with some Ray traced elements at 30hz  Resolution - native 4k at 30hz  Overall good. I think that's the best we'll get in terms of optimization from techland  everyone seems content with that so they'll probably start pushing new content as performance is fine as is.

One problem with games with enjoyable gameplay but bad stories is that they lose their replayability once a mechanically superior version of the same thing gets played. It's like using Windows 95; once 98 came out, there was no reason to go back to 95. Beautiful stories stand the test of time because we look past the dated gameplay or graphics to get to the story. Witcher 3 for instance is a really good example of this.  So, my question is how many people will be playing Dying Light 2 in 5 years?

I am only 23 hours in. My experience so far has been mixed. Overall though I think it is a great game. The parkour is great, better than the first imo. Story is good enough for me, the way they structured it definitely kept me engaged. At one point Hakon is just gone from the story when Lewan shows up. Went back to the Bazaar sometime later and everyone was gone, except for like one guy. It was weird, and also cool, like they were real people that packed up and left.   I also like the random stats on armor pieces and the special attacks that come with some weapons. You can actually do a build which is pretty cool.  My biggest complaints have to do with immersion and difficulty. Trees are growing out of the roofs, but it doesn't really look like they put enough soil on the roof to support these giant trees. Looks like they are just growing out of the roof. Maybe not big for some, but I definitely noticed it.   I was under the impression that at night, the streets would be packed with zombies, but that really is not the case. Also, night is not dark enough. And yes I turned shadow detail down on my TV. But I shouldn't have to, it makes some of the cut scenes to dark.   Sure there are Howlers and what not, but you can literally just out run everything. No Volatiles walking around at night, barely any Virals. Night is honestly a joke compared to DL.   And now the map. It is a beautiful map in all honesty, but there is no diversity it seems like. Just buildings with trees on the rooftops. Harrans atmosphere was amazing, so was The Following. The audio they used in the load screens really set the tone for me. Harran definitely made me feel isolated in another country, The Following brought more of a creepy/mystical ambiance to it. I get nothing from this map honestly.   Also, the red outline of the zombies from survivors sense really hits me wrong. It just seems so cheap. They all look like dummies. Not to mention most of the zombies look the same again.   Also no pvp. The whole reason for me leveling up and getting better gear was so I could fair better against the Night Hunter. What am I leveling up for now? To beat the zombies I can already beat easily on hard? Overall I am having a great time. Just some things I think they could of improved.   Imo, there should have been way more zombies on the ground, and less ways to get off the ground to the roofs, to really make it scary where you absolutely fear the ground like it is lava. And only when you have leveled up could you traverse the ground at night easily.

Plus one thing he didn't bring up: the game feels a bit more arcade-y than the original considering it has health bars, and enemy indicators during sneaking or chasing.  That said,  honestly I sorta like the health bars and the parkour/ combat foundation does feel just as great as the first game.  Plus the crafting system feels much better in this game. Plus I love the way they implemented Aiden's immunity as well as the progression. They are truly wonderful design changes that actively encourage you to explore and go fast, forcing you to play the game in its most enjoyable way.  Both feel like a unique  My only major concern about this game is that I haven't had *much* of a challenge yet, especially with the chases (I haven't seen any volatiles during chases yet).  I think that might be largely due to me being very early in the game though.  I haven't played enough to say if it's better than the original yet, but i can say that they certainly belong in the same tier.  Addition: after playing multiplayer and getting our cheeks clapped by a volatile while raiding a hospital, the game is a bunch of fun especially with multiplayer.  Combat is fun and does present a decent challenge while on hard difficulty.  I'm half sure that the only reason why he was even there to clap is in the first place was that we accidentally stayed in all the way until morning, but regardless the squealing that came out of our mouths while we frantically climbed a series of ladders to the safety of the UV was priceless.
